    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10839881129747232461"><b>A BIG NOVEL ABOUT A SMALL TOWN ...</b><br/><br/>When Barry Fairbrother dies in his early forties, the town of Pagford is left in shock.<br/><br/>Pagford is, seemingly, an English idyll, with a cobbled market square and an ancient abbey, but what lies behind the pretty façade is a town at war.<br/><br/>Rich at war with poor, teenagers at war with their parents, wives at war with their husbands, teachers at </span>
  <span id="freeText10839881129747232461" style="display:none"><b>A BIG NOVEL ABOUT A SMALL TOWN ...</b><br /><br />When Barry Fairbrother dies in his early forties, the town of Pagford is left in shock.<br /><br />Pagford is, seemingly, an English idyll, with a cobbled market square and an ancient abbey, but what lies behind the pretty façade is a town at war.<br /><br />Rich at war with poor, teenagers at war with their parents, wives at war with their husbands, teachers at war with their pupils ... Pagford is not what it first seems.<br /><br />And the empty seat left by Barry on the parish council soon becomes the catalyst for the biggest war the town has yet seen. Who will triumph in an election fraught with passion, duplicity and unexpected revelations?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10839881129747232461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Rowling does a lot of character development and little plot development, but whe<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">around the 300th page it picks up and moves fast. I was the same way. Rowling does a lot of character development and little plot development, but when the plot finally unfolds, it is all worth it. The way she grasps human nature... Ahh. It's really worth it, but it does seem slow as hell <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<a href="/questions/144286-describe-your-most-and-least-favorite">Describe your most and least favorite characters in this book?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_144286'><a id="like_count_community_question_144286" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/144286?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">26 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13497818-the-casual-vacancy">like</a></span>

</li>

<a href="/questions/144286-describe-your-most-and-least-favorite">6 years ago</a>
</li>

<a href="/questions/144286-describe-your-most-and-least-favorite">See all 30 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/11857119-aj"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1478026608i/11857119._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/11857119-aj">AJ</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">After I read this book, I returned it to the library and my kids asked about the author (they recognized JK Rowling). So I started ttelling them about<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">After I read this book, I returned it to the library and my kids asked about the author (they recognized JK Rowling). So I started ttelling them about the book and it came to me that my favorite character was Krystal Weedon and my least favorite was Fats. Krystal was put into such a desperate situation from how she was raised. Through no fault of her own, she was left to raise her baby brother and try to keep her mother from using heroin and losing the family. Plus, she had to go to school and deal with the death of Barry Fairbrother, her mentor and only ally. Fats, on the other hand, was a manipulative and calculating jerk. He took advantage of everyone's weaknesses and exploited them for his own enjoyment. I thought this was a great read!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_311431228" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311431228" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311431228?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311431228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18290976597746477872">J.K.Rowling gave a whole generation of kids an amazing fantasy to dream about (*). <br/><br/>Then she wrote this book that has many of the same elements, only without the safe haven of magic (**). Basically, this is a real world where <b>a strange man showing up at your family's doorstep at night is less likely to be a magical school groundskeeper but more likely your family's drug dealer</b> who, by the way, may not be adverse to beating and raping you for good measure.(***) <br/><br/><b>It's the world left for Dudley Dursl</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18290976597746477872" style="display:none">J.K.Rowling gave a whole generation of kids an amazing fantasy to dream about (*). <br><br>Then she wrote this book that has many of the same elements, only without the safe haven of magic (**). Basically, this is a real world where <b>a strange man showing up at your family's doorstep at night is less likely to be a magical school groundskeeper but more likely your family's drug dealer</b> who, by the way, may not be adverse to beating and raping you for good measure.(***) <br><br><b>It's the world left for Dudley Dursley and friends after Harry gets whisked away to magicland, and it ain't pretty.</b><blockquote>
  <i>(*) I confess - I'm a Potter fan, too. Just look at my t-shirt in my profile picture. I would also redo medical school in a heartbeat if only Hogwarts offered a med school curriculum.<br><br>(**) Abusive family, closed-mindedness, thinly veiled prejudice, bullying and constant threats - all that is just the beginning of the first Potter book. Later we have iron-pumping Dudley hang out at deserted playgrounds, taking pride in physically abusing small children. <br><br>(***) A tasteless joke to follow - well, drugs may be one plausible explanation for all that followed for the Potter kid, including Harry's fantastic magicland TRIP. Hehe.</i>
</blockquote>Okay, having got the Potter references and tasteless humor out of my system, I can start my actual review. <br>------------------------<br><i>The Casual Vacancy</i> is a book about the <b>pettiness and selfishness and often quite unintentional cruelty of mundane human life, which does not have to be dramatic or poignant or in any other way remarkable to be tragic.</b> It's not about any grand battle between good an evil, or any significant confrontations, or any remotely heroic feats - no, <b>it is about how small little seemingly insignificant things can combine into a depressing picture of everyday tragedy.</b><br><br>'Dark and gritty' <i>(the description that I've heard a few times about it)</i> it also isn't - it's simply realistic and does not shy away from life's unpleasantness. This is a book that is never about the destination (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it doesn't really have one, actually <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) but about the journey, cliché as it may sound.<br>-------------------------<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374909i/729260._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>What the town of Pagford would really like to be seen as.</i><br><br><i>The Casual Vacancy</i> is a book about a seemingly quaint English town of Pagford which, to the dismay of many well-meaning citizens, has a less than desirable area known as the Fields <i>(you know, one of those neighborhoods filled with drugs, drugs users, drug dealers, and terrifying poverty. And kids from there who go to the respectable town school, and some of whom grow up to be respectable, and some of whom punch other girls' teeth out. That kind of neighborhood)</i>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374909i/729261._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>What the rest of Padford sees the neighborhood of the Fields as.</i><br><br>So the well-meaning town officials are locked in the battle that involves either keeping the Fields or shuffling it off onto a neighboring town, and also whether to keep or to close a local methadone clinic. And when Barry, one of the town councillors, dies because of an unfortunately timed brain aneurysm, leaving a town council seat unoccupied, <b>the real ugly of small town politics rears its head. </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374909i/729262._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Add to the mix surly teenagers, drugs, sex, casual rape, bullying, domestic violence, lies, cheating, indifference, prejudice, self-mutilation, neglect, verbal abuse, desperation, almost-murder - and you have some idea of what <i>The Casual Vacancy</i> is about. And none of it is even remotely magical.<br><br>What I like most about this novel is that it's basically a <b>character study.</b> There's not that much plot, little action of any kind, and - *spoiler* - not that much resolution of existing conflicts by the end of the book. It is really just a sketch of a bit of small-town English society, quite nicely done. <i>
  <b>But hey - if character studies are not your cup of Earl Grey, you will definitely doze off over the 500-plus pages of this novel.</b>
</i> Luckily for me, this is a genre I enjoy.<blockquote>"<i>Life, for Colin, was one long brace against pain and disappointment, and everybody apart from his wife was an enemy until they had proven otherwise.</i>"</blockquote>We get to see the life in Pagford from the point of view of quite a few of its inhabitants. Normally I'd find that distracting, but here it's served its purpose - <b>making every character grey, nobody black-and-white.</b> Those who seemed destined to be 'the bad guys' in the first few chapters are not; they are very regular everyday people with regular flaws and charms, whose views are presented such that you see both flaws and reason in them. Those who seemed destined to be 'good guys', similarly, are not (see above). <b>Everyone is just an ordinary person, both likable and unlikable at the same time, and instantly recognizable as a 'real' person.</b><blockquote>"<i>He tried to give his wife pleasure in little ways, because he had come to realize, after nearly two decades together, how often he disappointed her in the big things. It was never intentional. They simply had very different notions of what ought to take up most space in life.</i>"</blockquote>Actually - and it must be my old age speaking - the person who I found to be the most antagonistic was a confused teenager searching for 'authenticity' with the utmost boneheadedness, I must add. <i>Get off my lawn, I scream, get off my lawn!</i> Everyone else, whether antagonistic or repulsive, felt firmly set on their unremarkable chosen road; Fats, on the other hand, was caught in a spiral of finding himself while quite deliberately hurting people around him, and I found it to be one of the most painful parts of the book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374909i/729263._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Authenticity, as Fats Wall, a middle-class suburban teenager, sees it.</i><br>-------------------------<br><b>J.K.Rowling is definitely NOT a one-hugely-popular-series wonder.</b> No, this woman can definitely write very well (and with properly placed punctuation!) Her prose is well-chosen, simple, and very non-distracting. As a writer, she never demands attention, never jumps out with a writing gimmick, never over-emphasizes her cleverness; she instead tells her story in an even and well-modulated voice, occasionally full of sadness, occasionally humorous but never overwhelming.<blockquote>"<i>‘Stone dead,’ said Howard, as though there were degrees of deadness, and the kind that Barry Fairbrother had contracted was particularly sordid.</i>"</blockquote>All in all, I thought it was a very well-executed and interesting book which will undoubtedly appeal to a much smaller audience than the Potter series, but among the ones that love it, this love will be well-deserved. I will be gladly waiting for anything else that Rowling chooses to write - and not only because I love Harry the wizard but because I'm sure now that she is a damn fine writer. <b>4.5 stars.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18290976597746477872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_283131659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283131659" />
    <a title="Mith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3620424-mith"><img alt="Mith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389091865p2/3620424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283131659?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mith" href="/user/show/3620424-mith">Mith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=slice-of-life">slice-of-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3620424-mith?shelf=goodish">goodish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283131659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11795259278439349061"><u>How (not) to read <b>The Casual Vacancy</b></u> :<br/><br/>1. <b>DON'T</b> read it <b>just because</b> it's written by JK Rowling.<br/>2. <b>DON'T</b> expect it to be like Harry Potter - i.e, magic stuff. (Read the blurb, nimrod)<br/>3. <b>DON'T</b> expect a murder mystery - it isn't one.<br/>4. <b>DON'T</b> read it if you are not comfortable with the fact that the woman who might have moulded your childhood, is writing about drugs, teen sex, prostitution, rape etc. - this book isn't for you.<br/>5. <b>DON'T</b> compare this with her previous works, for the love of God!<br/><br/>When it</span>
  <span id="freeText11795259278439349061" style="display:none"><u>How (not) to read <b>The Casual Vacancy</b></u> :<br /><br />1. <b>DON'T</b> read it <b>just because</b> it's written by JK Rowling.<br />2. <b>DON'T</b> expect it to be like Harry Potter - i.e, magic stuff. (Read the blurb, nimrod)<br />3. <b>DON'T</b> expect a murder mystery - it isn't one.<br />4. <b>DON'T</b> read it if you are not comfortable with the fact that the woman who might have moulded your childhood, is writing about drugs, teen sex, prostitution, rape etc. - this book isn't for you.<br />5. <b>DON'T</b> compare this with her previous works, for the love of God!<br /><br />When it was announced that Jo Rowling was coming out with a new book, comparisons with the Harry Potter series were inevitable. No matter how many times, and in how many interviews, Jo insisted over and over again that 'THIS IS NOT A HARRY POTTER BOOK NOR IS IT ANYTHING LIKE IT', a small part inside every fan, desperate for another book in the series (understandably), hoped for it anyway. <br /><br />(And so, when they were invariably proved wrong, there was backlash. Half the negative reviews on Goodreads are because it's 'not a Harry Potter book', which just pisses me off, so let's not go there)<br /><br />The Casual Vacancy is as steeped in reality as the Harry Potter books are removed from it. There's nothing fantastical about the story - it's simple and plain, told by holding nothing back.<br /><br />The characterization in this book is simply mind-blowing. Each and every one of the characters is so very <i>real</i> (I know this word's been thrown around a lot, but seriously, there's no other way to describe them) and has such depth! Through the course of the book, they are all ripped apart, dissected with unflinching honesty and laid bare for the readers to see. There are very few likable characters in the book, whom we can root for and hope that things work out for them eventually, but all of them end up earning our sympathies in the end. <br /><br />People have said that the characters in this book are not relatable at all. I disagree. Which one of us hasn't felt like a victim of the circumstances - hopeless, unloved, desperate, bullied, frustrated, at the end of our tether - at some point in our lives? We are all in the pages of this book. It's just that our stories are different. I think Jo has expertly managed to capture and show the best and the worst of human behaviour in the book; the worst being the inability to see beyond ourselves and our petty problems, while the best being our capability to change ourselves.<br /><br />Having said that, the biggest strength of the book is also, unfortunately, its biggest weakness. The setting up of the characters and their lives just takes too long. The plot, if you can call it that, begins to move ahead only after about 300 pages or so. Which was probably the reason why it took me this long to finish the book - I was plodding along until I was so caught up that I couldn't put the book down.<br /><br />The final few pages of the book were brilliant and typically Jo - sad, yet beautiful and touching at the same time. I don't understand why people say the ending was abrupt. For me, there was absolute and complete closure which left me smiling and feeling <i>content</i> long after I finished reading (Always a sign of a good book!).<br /><br />I would like to reiterate that 'The Casual Vacancy' <b>will not be for everybody</b>. Some of you will probably give up after the first hundred pages, others will crawl along because it's Jo, and in the hope that she might pull a rabbit out of her hat at the end and surprise you with something "magic-ky" (she doesn't). Quite a few of you will hate it, but that's probably because this not your genre and you only picked up this book because of Jo, so, in that case, it's not her, it's you.<br /><br />With this book, Jo has proved beyond a doubt that she can WRITE no matter what the genre is, that she still has that magical ability to tap into some part of us, connect with us and make us care, despite ourselves. However, unlike the Harry Potter books, this book will probably not be changing any lives any time soon (it certainly didn't change mine), but I'm glad to have read it, nonetheless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11795259278439349061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_283082570" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283082570" />
    <a title="Nina ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3785659-nina"><img alt="Nina ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326399105p2/3785659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283082570?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina ♥" href="/user/show/3785659-nina">Nina ♥</a>
      </span>

          is currently reading it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283082570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15616262230219270446"><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><br/><u><b> WARNING:</b></u> CAPSLOCK ABUSE. <div id="review_840168241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840168241" />
    <a title="Stephen King" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26367680-stephen-king"><img alt="Stephen King" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442438813p2/26367680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840168241?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen King" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen King" href="/user/show/26367680-stephen-king">Stephen King</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840168241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14855691280075948499">Not since Peyton Place has a writer so enthusiastically stripped the lace covers from small-town life to show the maggots of greed, lust, snobbery, and ambition squirming beneath—only Grace Metalious didn’t have Jo Rowling’s wicked sense of humor. The village of Pagford may be British, but the human foibles there are universal. Like the best social comedies, The Casual Vacancy features wit on top and outrage simmering below.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_283269126" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283269126" />
    <a title="Krys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2798856-krys"><img alt="Krys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329103793p2/2798856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283269126?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krys" href="/user/show/2798856-krys">Krys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=third-person-narrative">third-person-narrative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=long-length-book">long-length-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=english-setting">english-setting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283269126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10260205389876627941"><br/><br/>The Casual Vacancy = Mind Blowing. <br/><br/>There is a quote in J.K. Rowling's newly released book, The Casual Vacancy, that sums up the tone of this novel perfectly.<br/><br/><br/><i>"The mistake ninety-nine percent of humanity made, as far as Fats could see, was being ashamed of what they were, lying about it, trying to be somebody else. Honesty was Fats' currency, his weapon and defense. It frightened people when you were honest; it shocked them. Other people, Fats had discovered, were mired in embarrassment and preten</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10260205389876627941" style="display:none"><br /><br />The Casual Vacancy = Mind Blowing. <br /><br />There is a quote in J.K. Rowling's newly released book, The Casual Vacancy, that sums up the tone of this novel perfectly.<br /><br /><br /><i>"The mistake ninety-nine percent of humanity made, as far as Fats could see, was being ashamed of what they were, lying about it, trying to be somebody else. Honesty was Fats' currency, his weapon and defense. It frightened people when you were honest; it shocked them. Other people, Fats had discovered, were mired in embarrassment and pretense, terrified that their truths might leak out, but Fats was attracted by rawness, by everything that was ugly but honest, by the dirty things about which the likes of his father felt humiliated and disgusted. Fats thought a lot about messiahs and pariahs; about men labeled mad or criminal; noble misfits shunned by the sleepy masses."</i><br /><br /><br />Rowling's departure from the world of children's fantasy takes us in an entirely different direction - truth. This book focuses on the truths that exist between people in a community and, more importantly, the lies that tear them apart.<br /><br />The book starts with the death of Barry Fairbrother, a parish council member and much loved bloke about town. This leaves behind a casual vacancy - a much-sought-after spot on the town council. Barry's death shakes the town of Pagford to the foundation from the council to teens on his rowing team. Everyone has been affected. After his death Barry becomes the most omnipresent, oft-spoken-of-but-never-seen dead character since Rebecca haunted Manderley. Barry is a cause and a catalyst for everything that happens in this book.<br /><br />This book has been much maligned in reviews. I have read a number that decry it as boring, laughable, and a waste of time. This made the defiant part of me rise up - everyone hates it, so I have to like it. Strike that, I have to love it. For the record it's not a waste of time. Not one second. I have spent the last week reading it and I feel nothing but pleasure, and aching, gut-wrenching sorrow in tandem. To call this novel boring is a slap in Rowling's face. This novel is heartfelt and exciting. At first it's a heavily character driven romp, but then the story sweeps you off your feet and you just can't look away. Rowling touches on so many factors of the human condition within the pages. Emotions range from sorrow to laughter, passion to pain, and all of the spectra in between.<br /><br />I'm not sure what book the readers who claim it was boring were reading but, trust me, this wasn't it.<br /><br />My theory is that the people who gave up are the fans that she acquired who are not readers - those who read the books because they are "the in-thing" so they could talk about it with their peers. Their contempt for this book makes me think they are jaded, that they feel duped for buying this (or any) book when "It's not Harry Potter!".<br /><br />It's really their loss for giving up. They're missing an otherwise perfect literary experience.<br /><br />On that note, if you go in expecting Harry Potter you will be disappointed. I never thought I would say this but forget Harry Potter... Especially while reading this book. Harry Potter ended five years ago and since then Rowling has gifted us with this unexpectedly wonderful book. To bemoan the fact that it's not another book set in that world is a second slap in her face. Rowling is a writer. Was she not supposed to write another book after finishing THE series of her career? Absolutely not. If anything she has a hell of a lot to prove... and she proves her chops in The Casual Vacancy. Where else would you find jealousy, illegal drug usage, prostitution, teenage sex, LGBT relationships, parental abuse, neglect, cutting, hope, pedophilia, boy band obsession, social politics, power struggles, rape, fear, betrayal, unrequited love, (and more f-bombs than Sam Jackson drops in the average movie)... all together told in a beautiful language that makes the reader laugh, smile, and cry at unexpected turns? Sometimes within sentences of one another.<br /><br />Sound boring? It's not. Like I said, I don't know what book they were reading. I was completely riveted. And I sobbed at the end. Another truth.<br /><br />Sadly, there is no mention of magic, or Hogwarts, or wizards, witches, and house elves. It didn't need that - it has it's own unique brand of magic. It doesn't mention Muggles either, but it does delve heavily into their lives and the way they interact with one another.<br /><br />I am very impressed by Rowling's first adult book. It's literary, it's rough, it's blisteringly poignant. I will miss every single character.<br /><br />5 out of 5 stars. Brava, Rowling. You have made magic out of the extraordinary ordinary. Brava. <br /><br />- review courtesy of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliopunkkreads.com">www.bibliopunkkreads.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10260205389876627941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_313959923" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313959923" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313959923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18007468247572672267"><b>
  <u>28 Sept. '12</u>
</b><br/>I have to start by saying, that if you're expecting a (murder-)mystery novel; a plot submerged in conspiracies and political maneuverings, you will be sorely disappointed. If you're hoping to be transported to another magical adventure, you'll receive an even greater plummet back down to earth. <br/><br/>Look. If you're going to read this just because it has <b>JK Rowling</b>'s name splattered on there, <b>I strongly advise you to sit back, take a look at your computer screen, and read that book des</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18007468247572672267" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>28 Sept. '12</u>
</b><br>I have to start by saying, that if you're expecting a (murder-)mystery novel; a plot submerged in conspiracies and political maneuverings, you will be sorely disappointed. If you're hoping to be transported to another magical adventure, you'll receive an even greater plummet back down to earth. <br><br>Look. If you're going to read this just because it has <b>JK Rowling</b>'s name splattered on there, <b>I strongly advise you to sit back, take a look at your computer screen, and read that book description.</b> Does it sound like something you would enjoy? Does it attract you, in the least bit, at all? Or does it sound utterly boring you would rather do something more productive like watch <i>Desperate Housewives</i> back-to-back?<br><i>The Casual Vacancy</i> is everything the title and book cover promises it to be -- plain, straightforward, something so commonplace and <i>ordinary</i> that you wouldn't even notice it's there. This book doesn't try to impress anybody, I think looking at the drab red and white cover would tell you that much, but it <i>will</i> elicit some sort of reaction depending on how you interpret things.<br><br><i>The Casual Vacancy</i> reminds me a lot of the Australian drama film, <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0472582/" rel="nofollow noopener">2:37</a> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[which is a great, thought-provoking film, I must add <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Not because the plot is in any way similar, but rather that they provoke the same general reaction out of their audiences. Some parts are gritty, vile, and just plain offensive. <br>I've heard a few friends, read a few reviews, that mentioned how <b>Rowling</b> just seemed to arbitrarily slop down a bunch of cuss-words and sex scenes simply to get it across to her readers that <i>this is not Harry Potter, yo!</i> but I could not disagree more.<br>I think we have it all in our heads that <b>Rowling</b> is somehow pressured into differentiating this adult book of hers from her popular children's series, that we're assuming too much of her. Although it <i>does</i> seem sometimes that she's playing a game of <i>how many penis jokes can I slip into my adult-novel</i>, the real and horrible fact is that in the real world out there, people <i>do</i> cuss -- some much, <i>much</i> more than others. Teenagers <i>do</i> have unabashed sex -- sometimes in public places, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[if you think the sex scenes here are simply there for the sake of shock value, wait until you meet my having-sex-in-the-mosque friends! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and there <i>are</i> horrible, violent, incompetent parents out there.<br>Truthfully, <b>
  <u>I quite enjoyed the way Rowling gave distinct voices to her characters</u>
</b>. Some needed their mouths washed, some needed to grow a pair, some needed to be slapped across the face. It is a pity that her portrayal of real people is being watered down to her attempting to assure us this is an adult novel.<br><br>There is almost no theme that this book does <i>not</i> touch. There are unhappy marriages, failed relationships, dysfunctional families ... there are issues of depression and cutting, bullying, teenage delinquency -- in short, <b>this is a book about life</b>. This book is a drama. <b>
  <u>A slow-paced, character-driven drama</u>
</b>; an in-depth look, if you will, at the lives of multiple people. There is no <i>main character</i> in <i>The Casual Vacancy</i>. Instead, we look into the lives of a number of residents of Pagford, we make our own decisions on their personalities, which is one great strength of this novel, and we get to see reflections of our own society - perhaps our own selves - in the inhabitants of Pagford.<br><br>I have to admit, that contemporary fiction is not my genre. I find them dull, I find them boring, I find them - more often than not - shallow and poorly developed; poor, romanticized attempts of uncovering human nature and the world we live in.<br>But <b>
  <u>the way JK Rowling handled her characters is well-rounded and completely believable</u>
</b>. I know only too well, the same type of gossiping, drama-mongering women who secretly crave to be in the limelight. I know only too well the hypocrisies and selfishness of people who do not even ever mean to be hurtful.<br>Perhaps, <b>
  <u>the main reason I got through this novel and enjoyed it,</u>
</b> is because I simply find character studies fascinating - and that is, in large, what <i>The Casual Vacancy</i> is about. That said, I have no doubt that you will <b>utterly loathe</b> a majority - if not all - of these flawed, only too-real characters. It seems as if there was not a single inhabitant of Pagford with redeemable characteristics. And yet, you do get to sympathize with a few, every now and then. <br><br>The only character whose perspective we <i>didn't</i> get to really experience was perhaps the one who was most affected by Barry's death - his widow - whom, by the way other characters interact with her, I have come to despise. It may be a shock, but it isn't the physically abusive father who I hated the most, nor the good-for-nothing druggie mother <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[alright, maybe it comes to a tie <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> -- it was Mary, Barry's useless, whinging, annoying widow.<br><i>Cut her some slack,</i> I hear you say; <i>her husband just died.</i><br>It's a good thing we never got to see into her head, because I'm sure I would have found more reason to hate her. Her entire sadness and mourning is based upon selfish, egotistical reasons. She has no respect for her husband's efforts, nor the selfless work he so evidently found important. She also just walks around moping, breaking down every two seconds, doing things and making decisions that her husband would have no doubt disproved of.<br><br>Anyway. <b>
  <u>The head-jumping may be daunting</u>
</b> at first, and yes, some people will be highly turned off by this. I myself think that if it had been handled any other way, the continuous flow of the world would have been interrupted; like a sudden cut-to-black scene instead of a camera constantly filming events as they transpire, following one character from another as they pass each other by.<br>Also, <b>Rowling</b> sure likes her commas. But that is a minor detail, which I myself am often guilty of - so I don't find it too off-putting. I could complain that her sentences were often winding, multiple clauses abound, sometimes causing confusion and forcing re-reads - but that is the distinct style she so often uses, which is something I have come to enjoy; and once I got going, I almost didn't notice it.<br><br>But anyway. Enough about that. <b>What about the actual story?</b> Well, we begin with the death of Barry <s>Potter</s> Fairbrother. <br><b>**</b>As a sidenote -- it might seem, if you read the novel, that he was the only redeemable character in this entire tale; and yet the entire purpose of <i>The Casual Vacancy</i> was to show us how rotten and imperfect people are once we get inside their head. It is only a blessing we never got to experience Barry's perspective, otherwise our enchantment of him, I suspect, would have been rudely awakened.<b>**</b><br>Barry's death had an impact on the entire community of Pagford, for he had left an empty seat on the Parish council, and whoever takes his place may have a defining role on the future of a rehabilitation clinic and, by extension, the lives of people who depend on it.<br><br>And that is all there is to it, ladies and gentlemen. No mysterious murder plots, no sudden evil lord rising from the dead. Of course, we are entertained by the everyday dramas that you will find in such a small, close-knit society. There is sabotage, teenagers courting, MILFs on the prowl ... <b>
  <u>we have an abundance of little events that lead up to the final climax</u>
</b> of <i>The Casual Vacancy</i>: some would say, an unnecessary scene that acts as a turning point for our characters.<br>But in that scene, like the entire premise of the movie 2:37, we are reminded of the brutal truth of life; of how selfish and self-absorbed people are. Of how immersed we are in our own petty problems and little closed world, that we become so ignorant and shrug off the rest of the world. <br><br>It is a pity that something bad had to take place before we see some semblance of change in our characters - although some characters do not change at all. And some readers, I believe, will find this to their distaste. But for me, this is a simple fact of life. Some people <i>need</i> mistakes to learn from. Some people never learn at all. And <b>JK Rowling</b>'s beautiful, if brutal, portrayal of life; of actions and consequences; of people and society, would have been just another romanticized happily-ever-after if it had ended on any other note.<br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>27 Sept. '12</u>
</b><br>Alriiiight! I finally have a copy of this so I'm gonna say "screw it" to all the other books I'm currently reading and get started on this like, right now. JK Rowling, <i>bring it!</i><br><br><br><br><b> <u>5 July '12</u> </b><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1341322570l/13497818.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Is it just me, or don't you prefer JK Rowling's face as a cover?<br><br>I think we're part of some elaborate social psychology experiment. The hypothesis is that us suckers will buy any book written by such a long-anticipated author, even if it had a picture of dog turd on the cover.<br><br><br><br><b> <u>14 June '12</u> </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375290i/729829.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Not</i> final cover art??? You mean, she <i>won't</i> have a picture of her own face as the front cover of her novel?? I am disappointed.<br><br><br><br><b> <u>17 Apr. '12</u> </b><br>Look. I know we all love <b>J.K. Rowling</b> to bits and tiny pieces she would just die in our smothering worship ... but this book is not even out yet. HOW does it already have practically 5 stars?? <b>HOW?</b> Do people have access to a hidden manuscript that I am not aware of? Have people traveled back from the beautiful future just to put up their stars before everyone else?<br><br>
  <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="elfswood" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380227351i/681256.jpg" width="220 px" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203647971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10017498317661706492"><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578794903i/28761302._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Big bois. Long bois. Extra extra page bois.<br/><br/>Everyone's heard of them. The Libraries are full of them. But are they worth it?<br/><br/><b><u><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cXTQs28tKCk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click the link</a></u></b> for my video review of the big bois in my life.</blockquote>The Written Review:<b>Small town gossip, big town problems</b><br/><br/>By no exaggeration, the entire community hinged on Barry Fairbrother. He was the glue, the tape, the old piece of string. <br/><br/>And, they are left scrambling to hold things together when he unexpectedly passed. <br/><br/>Why? Because the<b> entire idyllic town is festering over</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10017498317661706492" style="display:none"><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578794903i/28761302._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Big bois. Long bois. Extra extra page bois.<br><br>Everyone's heard of them. The Libraries are full of them. But are they worth it?<br><br><b><u><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cXTQs28tKCk" rel="nofollow noopener">Click the link</a></u></b> for my video review of the big bois in my life.</blockquote>The Written Review:<b>Small town gossip, big town problems</b><br><br>By no exaggeration, the entire community hinged on Barry Fairbrother. He was the glue, the tape, the old piece of string. <br><br>And, they are left scrambling to hold things together when he unexpectedly passed. <br><br>Why? Because the<b> entire idyllic town is festering over a cesspool </b>of drugs, prostitution, self harm, rape, class divisions, abuse and sexism. <br><br>Told through ever changing narrators, we see just how Barry Fairbrother held their families - their community - together through his kindness and willingness to care. <br><br> And without him, the whole town begins to crumble. Will they pull everything together? Or will everything be lost forever? <br><br>Whoa. <b> This one was intense</b> - not at all what I expected from JK Rowling. <br><br>It was still good - just completely unexpected. <br><br>The characters were well fleshed out and the plot was absolutely riveting. It's a bit like watching a train wreck. <br><br>So many people, so many ways to uniquely ruin lives. <br><br>After learning all that Barry did, <b>I'm surprised that his aneurysm hadn't come earlier.</b> <br><br>The book did get to be a bit overwhelming - there's only so much I can take. About 3/4, the book got a bit overwhelming for me...<br><br>It ends on a semi-positive note, with a hint of a hope that things will get better - which felt fairly realistic. <br><br>I'm glad I read this one but I don't think I'll pick up a copy.<br><br> Just as a note, if you are looking for something with the harry potter vibe... this is not it. <br><br>The teens in this book are not idyllic or innocent. They are already well versed in abuse, neglect, drugs and sex, courtesy of their upbringing.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments:</b><br>Tom Hollander did a pretty good job of distinguishing the characters through inflections and mannerisms. With such a large cast, I think there needed to be a bit more characterization to help tell them apart.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282893305?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282893305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11090762307641403879"><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/11/the-casual-vacancy-by-jk-rowling.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Find more of my controversial reviews at Scott Reads It</a><br/><br/>After rereading my review of The Casual Vacancy I realized it sounded sloppy and very unprofessional. I decided to edit my entire review and start from scratch. <br/><br/>I had such high expectations for The Casual Vacancy and I was extremely letdown. I'll admit that the only reason that I read this book is because I adore J.K. Rowling and her Harry Potter series. I was so excited to read a new J.K. Rowling book that I didn't care that The Casual Vaca</span>
  <span id="freeText11090762307641403879" style="display:none"><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2012/11/the-casual-vacancy-by-jk-rowling.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my controversial reviews at Scott Reads It</a><br /><br />After rereading my review of The Casual Vacancy I realized it sounded sloppy and very unprofessional. I decided to edit my entire review and start from scratch. <br /><br />I had such high expectations for The Casual Vacancy and I was extremely letdown. I'll admit that the only reason that I read this book is because I adore J.K. Rowling and her Harry Potter series. I was so excited to read a new J.K. Rowling book that I didn't care that The Casual Vacancy was nothing like her Harry Potter series. (That's not to say that I secretly wished that The Casual Vacancy was some sort of spin off or sequel to Harry Potter.)<br /><br />Though J.K. Rowling's writing style is evident in The Casual Vacancy, nevertheless reading The Casual Vacancy felt like a form of torture. I lacked any emotional attachment or connection with the characters in The Casual Vacancy. The only emotions towards the characters in this book were repulsion and extreme distaste. The political structure of this book was portrayed in a manner that was unappealing and tedious. <br /><br />I felt like The Casual Vacancy unnecessarily dirty and vulgar. I believe that J.K. Rowling was trying to differentiate from her children's books by adding rape, pedophilia, sex scenes, and adult content. How many times can you drop the f-bomb before it becomes irritating? <br /><br />It is truly alarming how 5 star reviews I have seen that were written by people who have never even read The Casual Vacancy. It truly defeats the purpose of Goodreads to review and rate a book you have never even read. <br /><br />I wish I had a better experience reading The Casual Vacancy. The Casual Vacancy was very dull and I struggled to read a few chapters. One day I hope I will attempt to finish The Casual Vacancy but for now I'm marking it as DNF. </span>

<div id="review_311442584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311442584" />
    <a title="Haleema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema"><img alt="Haleema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402430795p2/4336293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311442584?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haleema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haleema" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema">Haleema</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311442584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14958163978803263127">Listen, people. I'm not <i>extremely</i> excited for this book because it's not fantasy. And I don't mean Harry Potter's continuation. Please, as much as I loved HP, I don't need to read about his kids because I cannot get myself to give a damn. The end is the end. I can't see how she can continue that series.<br/><br/>Rowling has said that this book is completely different from what HP had given us. It's dark, dreary, a bit personal, and is solely for adults. And even though I love, love, <i>love</i> HP, I didn't preo</span>
  <span id="freeText14958163978803263127" style="display:none">Listen, people. I'm not <i>extremely</i> excited for this book because it's not fantasy. And I don't mean Harry Potter's continuation. Please, as much as I loved HP, I don't need to read about his kids because I cannot get myself to give a damn. The end is the end. I can't see how she can continue that series.<br /><br />Rowling has said that this book is completely different from what HP had given us. It's dark, dreary, a bit personal, and is solely for adults. And even though I love, love, <i>love</i> HP, I didn't preorder this book or went completely crazy about being the first to grab it. In fact, I won't mind spending a few months waiting to read it.<br /><br />But J.K. ROWLING IS WRITING ANOTHER BOOK! WE GET TO HEAR ABOUT SOME ASPECTS OF HER PERSONAL LIFE THAT I WAS TOO LAZY TO GOOGLE/STALK MYSELF! AND I'M SORRY FOR USING CAPLOCKS WHEN I CAN USE EXCLAMATION MARKS BUT THAT DOESN'T DO JUSTICE FOR THE FACT THAT ROWLING IS WRITING ANOTHER BOOK.</span>

<div id="review_425822227" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425822227" />
    <a title="Nilesh Kashyap" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6361703-nilesh-kashyap"><img alt="Nilesh Kashyap" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424881610p2/6361703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425822227?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilesh Kashyap" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilesh Kashyap" href="/user/show/6361703-nilesh-kashyap">Nilesh Kashyap</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425822227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17959863339662437649"><b>6.11</b> A casual vacancy is deemed to have occurred:<br/>(a) when a local councillor fails to make his declaration of acceptance of office within the proper time; or<br/>(b) when his notice of resignation is received; or<br/>(c) on the day of his death …<br/>Charles Arnold-Baker<br/><i>Local Council Administration</i>,<br/>Seventh Edition<br/><br/><br/>Barry Fairbrother, local councillor of Pagford lay dead on the ground in pool of his own vomit. His death creates a situation called '<u>
  <i>casual vacancy</i>
</u>'. A lot of people of people are willing to fill</span>
  <span id="freeText17959863339662437649" style="display:none"><b>6.11</b> A casual vacancy is deemed to have occurred:<br />(a) when a local councillor fails to make his declaration of acceptance of office within the proper time; or<br />(b) when his notice of resignation is received; or<br />(c) on the day of his death …<br />Charles Arnold-Baker<br /><i>Local Council Administration</i>,<br />Seventh Edition<br /><br /><br />Barry Fairbrother, local councillor of Pagford lay dead on the ground in pool of his own vomit. His death creates a situation called '<u>
  <i>casual vacancy</i>
</u>'. A lot of people of people are willing to fill Barry’s vacant seat on the parish council. Thus, begins the story of a small English town called, Pagford. <br />A part of Pagford is ‘<i>the fields</i>’, pretty fucked up place. Many members at the council never accepted the fields and its people as their own and now they want to separate <i>that filthy place</i> from their own Pagford. And now this task seems much easy than ever, since Barry is dead. Barry, who dedicated his entire life to make people realise that <i>the fields</i> has always been part of Pagford.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>
    <i>'The Rowling Experience'</i>
  </b>
</u><br /><br />This is the first time I have read a novel by J. K. Rowling. Yup! No Harry Potter for me. So unlike many fan of hers, I have no reason to measure the goodness of her other novels against the scale, based on Harry Potter novels.<br />I read this book for simply what it is, not because I have been missing Harry Potter or her writing. I don’t know, how good is she as a YA-fiction writer, but she is damn good as a writer of an adult and a realistic novel. <br />What I liked most about her writing is characterization, <u>this novel is all about characters</u> and each and every character is so well developed that you can connect with their thoughts and action, moreover you can recognize the characters from their dialogues without any reference to speaking person. Need I say more about her writing skills?<br /><br /><u>
  <b>
    <i>'The Casual Vacancy: As It Is'</i>
  </b>
</u><br /><br />Adults Only! For some reason when I heard that it’s going to be an adult novel, I conjured up an image of a mature book, with some deep embedded thoughts and thought provoking writing. Basically, mature. <br />Well, surprise! This is seriously an adult novel. Many reviewers say that Rowling has tried to make this adult by unnecessarily using all kind of <i>dirty words</i>. Word count of <u>few</u> such 'dirty words'<br />Arse: 5 times	<br />Bloody: 61 times<br />Fuck (my favourite, and given the count looks like Rowling’s favourite too): 214 times<br />Shag: 13 times<br />Wank: 2 times<br />Shit (second favourite): 43 times <br /><br />But the thing is that these words have very less or no contribution in making this an adult novel. Strip this novel of these words and it will still remain very much adult as it was before. It is the issues and situation that makes it what it is. And these words are not forced in any of the character’s mouth; they say it like they own it. <br /><u>Moreover, whatever is being termed here as adult, is fucking reality of our society</u>.<br /><br /><b>Things that other reviewers have said</b> (mostly those who have read around 50–pages and therefore <i>abandoned</i>):<br />-crappy story of a town rocked by death of some Barry Fairbrother<br />-no likeable character<br />-simply not interesting; in other words, nothing like Harry Potter<br /><br />The story of this book is <u>not</u> about Pagford and how it was affected by Barry’s death and definitely not about Barry. The death of Barry is just a pretext of starting a story.<br />For the first 50 pages only thing that happens is introduction of various families (characters) living in Pragford. These introduction are connected through passing message of Barry Fairbrother’s death. So in these pages what one will come across is that; Barry is dead. Rating the book at this point is like rating a YA-novel after 10-15 pages. <br /><br />If you ask about the plot of the story, then I’m afraid I can’t tell you much because this is not an exactly plot driven story. Those who think of this book as such have complained in their review that ‘ending is abrupt’. Well, the ending is not abrupt, but my friend, <u>you were holding the wrong thread of the story</u>. <br />This is more like <u>character-driven story</u>, this is all about characters, as I told before. This story is about the people of Pagford, who have constructed themselves in all the wrong ways possible and this story make them realise this fact and gives them a once in a lifetime opportunity by destroying them, so that they can start all over again. When they restart, that is the end.<br /><br />No likeable character. I disagree! <br />Well, there are many likeable and very very interesting characters, but if you meant that there is no protagonist, whom you can cling to throughout the story, then only I can agree.<br />Consider this as a story with no protagonist or many protagonists. I don’t consider anybody in this story as an antagonist because this is a politics based story and in politics everybody is right and everybody is wrong.<br /><br />I agree that starting of the story is not at all interesting. Reason: there are many characters, actually too many and everyone is important, so this leads to lot of confusion and it takes time to settle this confusion. Every time a character give their following appearance, it is hard to remember whose son/wife/husband they are and whether they are anti-field or pro-field. But, once I got accustomed to characters, setting and their relation to everybody, this story flowed better than ever.<br /><br />I liked Rowling's writing so much that I can say: Very much magical, even without magic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17959863339662437649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_423840174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423840174" />
    <a title="Anachronist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5587874-anachronist"><img alt="Anachronist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362432728p2/5587874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423840174?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anachronist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anachronist" href="/user/show/5587874-anachronist">Anachronist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423840174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10068503084676297966">Synopsis:<br/><br/>When Barry Fairbrother dies suddenly of aneurism in his early forties, leaving his family and a lot of unfinished issues behind, the town of Pagford is in shock. He was a well-known councilor and a coach of the local female rowing team. He was also a man with a mission. Who will fill his shoes? Will his death benefit his allies or his enemies?<br/>Surprisingly there are more than one or two token candidates. Pagford, seemingly an English sleepy town like many others, with a cobbled market sq</span>
  <span id="freeText10068503084676297966" style="display:none">Synopsis:<br /><br />When Barry Fairbrother dies suddenly of aneurism in his early forties, leaving his family and a lot of unfinished issues behind, the town of Pagford is in shock. He was a well-known councilor and a coach of the local female rowing team. He was also a man with a mission. Who will fill his shoes? Will his death benefit his allies or his enemies?<br />Surprisingly there are more than one or two token candidates. Pagford, seemingly an English sleepy town like many others, with a cobbled market square and an ancient abbey, becomes a war zone and, like in every war, there will be casualties. Who will prevail? Is it important at all?<br /><br />My impressions:<br /><br />First of all let me state the obvious: hearing the name of J.K. Rowling you will immediately think ‘Harry Potter’ even if you haven’t read any of the books or haven’t seen the movies. But HP series was finished some time ago and now Ms Rowling decided to branch out. I am far from criticizing her for that, let me just say it was a very bold move, rejecting a genre which made you famous, renowned and super-rich, trying something entirely new and different. I grant it, she could afford that little experiment without breaking out into a financial sweat, a rare luxury among authors. My question is rather why it was done the way it was done especially that it could have been done practically any way?<br /><br />My first surprise: the new book was still published under the name of J.K. Rowling. Let’s face it – whether the author likes it or not that name belongs firmly to Harry Potter. Using it to market a contemporary fiction novel for adults is like trying to sell e.g. BMW shoes or Manolo Blahnik computers. Of course it has its short-term advantages: plenty of people have bought the book out of sheer curiosity or loyalty so I suppose the publisher and the author will make a nice, fat profit, no problem. Still most of those casual readers will be confused and disenchanted at best, getting not exactly what they have expected or used to expect. I suppose next time they won’t fall for the magic name alone.<br /><br />The novel itself is a solid piece of writing, planned and executed decently well, but the topic isn’t either fresh or original, let alone ground-breaking. I am not an especially well-read person in English literature and even I have read many similar position by Kate Atkinson or Sue Townsend; I can even add Agatha Christie to the bunch here, and I must say their books were actually better – funnier, more edgy. Do not expect in The Casual Vacancy any magic, even of the metaphorical kind, or fireworks of humour and wisdom. While reading it I didn’t feel that intense urge to find out what happened next, or to devour the book as soon as possible. It was a tepid story set in a banal, industrial-grey world; after finishing it I could shrug my shoulders and move on. I related to none of the characters, I didn’t hate anybody in particular, I am not curious what will happen to them in the future. If I have to be honest I could live without meeting them at all.<br /><br />I suppose I would be far more comfortable if the book was published under an alias. Now it seems to me that Ms Rowling decided to minimize any risk and to capitalize shamelessly on her previous success, selling readers something which is supposedly connected to the HP series but in reality as far away from those books as it can only be. Only after the lecture of reviews or the book itself you see you have been conned. . Had this one been penned by a debut author, without all that glamour of a world-famous name, it would have still been published but I am sure it would have also passed unnoticed and would have been forgotten soon.<br /><br />By the way would it be such a bad idea to write something new (heck, even starting a new series) for adults but with fantasy elements included? Do only kids deserve a bit of fun? Taking into account how many mature readers have enjoyed the adventures of Harry and his friends, not to mention his enemies (yours truly among them) it seems like a completely rhetorical question, right?<br /><br />Final verdict:<br /><br />A decent novel about contemporary Britain but nothing outstanding you must or should read or you miss out on an important book. Rowling has said pre-emptively: ‘ I'm a writer and I will write what I want to write.' Ok, fine. I am a reader and I will read what I want to read. Not something like this one, though.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10068503084676297966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_424215227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424215227" />
    <a title="Issy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6114416-issy"><img alt="Issy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314173160p2/6114416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/424215227?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Issy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Issy" href="/user/show/6114416-issy">Issy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424215227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14849615028358748193">This book is utterly heartbreaking, but real, gritty, and slightly sickening. <br/><br/>I had no idea what this novel was going to be about when I bought it yesterday. Being 17, I have grown up living and breathing Harry Potter. It is correct to assume that this novel is an utter contrast to the Harry Potter series. But I think it is a most naive error to try to compare the two works. It goes to JK Rowlings credit that she can produce such varied pieces, and write them so well!<br/><br/>I love this novel. I find th</span>
  <span id="freeText14849615028358748193" style="display:none">This book is utterly heartbreaking, but real, gritty, and slightly sickening. <br /><br />I had no idea what this novel was going to be about when I bought it yesterday. Being 17, I have grown up living and breathing Harry Potter. It is correct to assume that this novel is an utter contrast to the Harry Potter series. But I think it is a most naive error to try to compare the two works. It goes to JK Rowlings credit that she can produce such varied pieces, and write them so well!<br /><br />I love this novel. I find that I am attracted to it for the same reasons I am attracted to Steinbeck's novella Of Mice and Men: it is fast paced, never boring, develops characters well, and most importantly regularly sheds truthful insights into the workings of the human mind, and how we perceive life. <br /><br />Basically, it cuts through the bullshit. It doesn't matter how pretty the prose one may read in a novel today, if you can find a book like this, one that will rip your heart open and expose it for the world to see, making you consider who you are as a person, you are lucky.<br /><br />Rowling is a brilliant writer, and with such fluency and articulation she shows her characters to be three-dimensional, giving the reader no reason to hate any of them, but no reason to love them either. My favourite character would probably be Krystal, although I grew to love both Tessa Wall and Sukhvinder Jawanda increasingly. Rowling produced such strong characters in these three women, writing them so non-stereotypically, giving them unique viewpoints it's hard to believe that they were strictly fictional. In Samantha Mollison you found a 'Emma Bovary' type, types that I often have love/hate relationships with (a women so bored of her conventional married life, that she acts outrageously to fill the void inside of her.)<br />The only male character I had any fondness towards was Andrew Price and perhaps his poor younger brother. I found them both endearing, and could relate to their struggles. <br />What I like most about how she wrote her characters was the way she saved judgement; she let readers weigh up each characters strengths and weaknesses, to make a decision on how they felt about them theirselves.<br /><br />Living on and off in a country town for 10 years, I found that Rowling's portrayal of country life was extremely accurate. The narrow-mindedness that is often expressed, the idea that there is no life that matters outside the town, the loyalty and defensiveness around it, the nosy community, the hunger for gossip, the rebellious adolescents.<br /><br />In the end, I don't think this book as a particular agenda. I think in its brilliant 500 pages, its sole purpose is to portray life as it is. It's direct truthfulness stuns me. Those who criticise this novel for its 'dark themes' or 'foul language' simply remind me of Howard and Shirley Mollison, who don't believe terrible and dirty things actually happen in their own little universe and if they do, they are more than happy to write them off. <br /><br />Bad things happen. So do good things. If you're unable to stomach this, and want Harry to defeat dark wizard after dark wizard without failure, this novel isn't for you. If you're able to accept that life isn't always sunshine and lollipops, I guarantee you will be able to relate to, and even enjoy (what a thought!) this novel. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14849615028358748193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1708108686" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1708108686" />
    <a title="Mansuriah Hassan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26126450-mansuriah-hassan"><img alt="Mansuriah Hassan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580314850p2/26126450.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mansuriah Hassan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mansuriah Hassan" href="/user/show/26126450-mansuriah-hassan">Mansuriah Hassan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408704202" href="/book/show/13578351-the-casual-vacancy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26126450-mansuriah-hassan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
